The same generated CSV includes `uiuc_static_reynolds_point` rows derived from the UIUC static `RPM CT CP` files. The Re columns are proxy values using 25 C air and the project's representative chord convention; use the ratios and slopes as trend anchors, not as exact UIUC-reported Reynolds values.

| UIUC static prop | RPM range | Re75 proxy range | tip Mach range | CT high/low Re | CP high/low Re | Q/T high/low Re | CT slope per 100k Re |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| [DA4052 5x3.75 3-blade](https://m-selig.ae.illinois.edu/props/volume-2/data/da4052_5x3.75_3b_static_1204ga.txt) | 1478-7947 | 3745-20136 | 0.028-0.153 | 1.074 | 0.809 | 0.753 | 0.0431 |
| [NR640 5in 15deg 3-blade](https://m-selig.ae.illinois.edu/props/volume-2/data/nr640_5_15deg_3b_static_0696md.txt) | 1482-9898 | 3756-25080 | 0.028-0.190 | 1.333 | 0.855 | 0.641 | 0.1477 |
| [MicroInvent 5x4 3-blade](https://m-selig.ae.illinois.edu/props/volume-2/data/mit_5x4_static_0362rd.txt) | 1596-6396 | 4043-16206 | 0.031-0.123 | 1.004 | 0.972 | 0.968 | -0.0138 |
| [APC SF 10x4.7](https://m-selig.ae.illinois.edu/props/volume-1/data/apcsf_10x4.7_static_kt0835.txt) | 2377-6528 | 24092-66165 | 0.091-0.251 | 1.227 | 1.232 | 1.004 | 0.0609 |

Two modeling notes fall out of this: first, a density ratio below 1 raises required RPM roughly by `1/sqrt(rho_ratio)` for the same thrust, which quickly eats motor/battery headroom at high density altitude. Second, cold air lowers speed of sound, so a fixed max RPM can move closer to the compressibility onset even though cold dense air helps thrust.

## Wind and turbulence sanity

References: [pyfly Dryden implementation](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/eivindeb/pyfly/master/pyfly/dryden.py), [open UAV wind modeling survey](https://arxiv.org/abs/1905.09954), and [ICAS 2020 quadrotor adverse-situations CFD](https://www.icas.org/icas_archive/ICAS2020/data/papers/ICAS2020_0482_paper.pdf). Generated wind CSV: `docs/data/wind_gust_dryden_reference.csv`.

The Dryden rows use the common low-altitude formulas at 6 m altitude and take `wind20` equal to the scenario wind speed. The current model rows estimate target-gust RMS from the scaled dirty-air burble plus Dryden target before vehicle response and first-order filtering; the runtime implementation drives the Dryden part with a reproducible colored-noise process.

Generated wind packet CSV: `docs/data/wind_gust_calibration_packet.csv`. It condenses 632 `wind_gust_packet_*` rows into current-vs-Dryden intensity scans, spectral-shape scans, ICAS hover-gust CT rows, and crosschecks mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv`.

| Wind packet item | value | read as |
|---|---:|---|
| current wind scan rows | `12` | dirty-air/wind-speed grid from the generated reference |
| ICAS hover-gust CT rows | `12` | 4319/6528 rpm, no-wind and five gust directions |
| representative RMS X/Y | `1.653/0.843 m/s` | `wind=10 m/s`, `dirtyAir=1.5` current target |
| representative RMS ratio X/u Y/w | `0.86/0.84x` | close to low-altitude Dryden intensity |
| current gust corner | `1.373 Hz` | much faster than Dryden `u/w` poles |
| Dryden u/w poles | `0.037/0.265 Hz` | low-altitude shape reference at 6 m |
| 1 Hz shape ratio u/w | `21.9/1.86x` | RMS can match while spectrum is too fast |
| current X RMS / Dryden u range | `0.142..1.047x` | full generated dirty-air/wind grid |
| current corner / Dryden u-pole range | `13.6..78.8x` | one-pole gust filter is high-frequency biased |
| ICAS CT change envelope | `-131..+120%` | direct rotor-thrust effect, not just wind-field RMS |

| wind | dirtyAir | current gust RMS X/Y/Z | current peak X/Y/Z | phase periods A/B/C | tau gust/mean | Dryden sigma u/w | RMS ratio X/u Y/w | Dryden time u/w |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 5 m/s | 0.75 | 0.421/0.213/0.421 m/s | 1.062/0.497/1.057 m/s | 2.035/1.956/2.552 s | 0.147/0.250 s | 0.965/0.500 m/s | 0.44/0.43 | 8.629/1.200 s |
| 5 m/s | 1.50 | 0.842/0.425/0.841 m/s | 2.123/0.994/2.113 m/s | 1.561/1.601/1.733 s | 0.116/0.355 s | 0.965/0.500 m/s | 0.87/0.85 | 8.629/1.200 s |
| 10 m/s | 0.75 | 0.826/0.422/0.826 m/s | 2.000/0.956/1.993 m/s | 1.616/1.670/2.157 s | 0.147/0.340 s | 1.930/1.000 m/s | 0.43/0.42 | 4.315/0.600 s |
| 10 m/s | 1.50 | 1.653/0.843/1.652 m/s | 4.000/1.911/3.986 m/s | 1.302/1.404/1.542 s | 0.116/0.445 s | 1.930/1.000 m/s | 0.86/0.84 | 4.315/0.600 s |
| 15 m/s | 0.75 | 1.233/0.631/1.232 m/s | 2.939/1.414/2.929 m/s | 1.340/1.457/1.869 s | 0.147/0.430 s | 2.895/1.500 m/s | 0.43/0.42 | 2.876/0.400 s |
| 15 m/s | 1.50 | 2.466/1.262/2.465 m/s | 5.878/2.829/5.858 m/s | 1.117/1.250/1.389 s | 0.116/0.535 s | 2.895/1.500 m/s | 0.85/0.84 | 2.876/0.400 s |

| wind 10 m/s dirtyAir | current gust corner | Dryden u/w pole | corner over Dryden u/w | shape ratio at 0.5 Hz u/w | shape ratio at 1 Hz u/w |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 0.75 | 1.081 Hz | 0.037/0.265 Hz | 29.3x/4.1x | 12.3x/1.21x | 19.9x/1.69x |
| 1.50 | 1.373 Hz | 0.037/0.265 Hz | 37.2x/5.2x | 12.8x/1.25x | 21.9x/1.86x |

| ICAS hover gust case | gust direction | CT no wind | CT in gust | CT change |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 4319 rpm, 10 m/s gust | -90 deg | 0.00822 | -0.00258 | -131% |
| 4319 rpm, 10 m/s gust | -45 deg | 0.00822 | 0.00115 | -86% |
| 4319 rpm, 10 m/s gust | 0 deg | 0.00822 | 0.00876 | 7% |
| 4319 rpm, 10 m/s gust | 45 deg | 0.00822 | 0.01678 | 104% |
| 4319 rpm, 10 m/s gust | 90 deg | 0.00822 | 0.01810 | 120% |
| 6528 rpm, 10 m/s gust | -90 deg | 0.00831 | 0.00264 | -68% |
| 6528 rpm, 10 m/s gust | -45 deg | 0.00831 | 0.00388 | -53% |
| 6528 rpm, 10 m/s gust | 0 deg | 0.00831 | 0.00880 | 6% |
| 6528 rpm, 10 m/s gust | 45 deg | 0.00831 | 0.01155 | 39% |
| 6528 rpm, 10 m/s gust | 90 deg | 0.00831 | 0.01181 | 42% |

The Dryden component now carries the physical low-altitude length scales and sigma targets as colored noise, while the remaining deterministic burble is deliberately reduced and kept as obstacle/dirty-air feel. A future full Dryden/Von Karman shaping filter would be a cleaner spectral target, but the wind field is no longer driven only by sine excitation.

## ZJU ground-effect and motor calibration anchor

Source: [Ground-effect-controller supplementary material](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ZJU-FAST-Lab/Ground-effect-controller/master/README.md); paper page: [arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.19424). Generated ZJU model CSV: `docs/data/zju_ground_effect_model_reference.csv`.

| Parameter row | Source context | k_T, N/rpm^2 | k, N/(rad/s)^2 | Q/T, m |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| ZJU single-rotor platform kT | single-rotor platform | 4.008e-08 | 3.655e-06 | 0.0159 |
| ZJU quadrotor platform kT | quadrotor platform | 3.784e-08 | 3.451e-06 | 0.0169 |
| ZJU real-flight hover kT | real flight by hovering | 4.296e-08 | 3.917e-06 | 0.0149 |

The same ZJU table reports ground-effect coefficients `g1=0.018`, `g2=0.007`, `g3=-0.337`, `g4=0.041`, `g5=0.065`, rotor drag `dx=0.397` and `dy=0.330` N/(m/s), mass `1.696` kg, and inertia `Ix/Iy/Iz=0.007/0.008/0.012` kg*m^2.

The ZJU paper model is mapped as `F_G(h)=g2/(h^2+g1)` for additional thrust fraction and `M_G(h)=g5*h/(h^2+g3*h+g4)^2` for the leveling-torque shape. The table below compares that same physical clearance against the current `racingQuad` ground-effect multiplier.

| h/R racingQuad | height | current thrust | ZJU formula thrust | current extra / ZJU extra | ZJU torque shape / peak |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 0.5 | 0.032 m | 1.161x | 1.385x | 0.42x | 0.030 |
| 1.0 | 0.064 m | 1.144x | 1.332x | 0.43x | 0.105 |
| 1.5 | 0.095 m | 1.127x | 1.271x | 0.47x | 0.270 |
| 2.0 | 0.127 m | 1.112x | 1.215x | 0.52x | 0.560 |
| 3.0 | 0.191 m | 1.084x | 1.135x | 0.62x | 0.997 |
| 4.0 | 0.254 m | 1.060x | 1.089x | 0.67x | 0.583 |

| Low/high comparison | sqrt(T) prediction | measured dx | measured dy | measured/predicted dx/dy | current extra drag proxy at 10 m/s |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| ZJU 0.10 m / 2.00 m rotor-drag ratio | 0.949 | 0.596 | 0.618 | 0.629/0.651 | 0.559 N at 0.10 m / 0.000 N at 2.00 m |

Important semantic split: ZJU's drag row is an identified rotor-drag coefficient ratio, while the current Java path adds a separate near-ground lateral drag force. The signs can coexist only if the latter is intentionally modeling airframe/ground cushion interaction rather than rotor-drag coefficient growth.

## Ground-effect shape comparison

Reference formula source: [gym-pybullet-drones BaseAviary.py](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/utiasDSL/gym-pybullet-drones/main/gym_pybullet_drones/envs/BaseAviary.py)

| Preset | height | boost | current @1R | current @2R | current @4R | gym-pybullet CF2 @1R/@2R/@4R |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | 0.600 m | 0.180 | 1.144 | 1.112 | 1.060 | 1.711/1.178/1.044 |
| cinewhoop | 0.750 m | 0.240 | 1.216 | 1.194 | 1.153 | 1.711/1.178/1.044 |
| heavyLift | 1.200 m | 0.120 | 1.096 | 1.075 | 1.040 | 1.711/1.178/1.044 |
| hexLift | 1.050 m | 0.110 | 1.089 | 1.070 | 1.040 | 1.711/1.178/1.044 |
| octoLift | 1.150 m | 0.100 | 1.081 | 1.064 | 1.036 | 1.711/1.178/1.044 |
| coaxialX8 | 1.150 m | 0.100 | 1.081 | 1.064 | 1.036 | 1.711/1.178/1.044 |

The current model is intentionally capped and smooth. Compared with the CF2 reference shape, it is much softer at `h=R` but similar by `h=4R` for the racing preset. Treat this as a shape sanity check, not a direct coefficient transplant, because Crazyflie-scale props and FPV 5-inch props operate at different Reynolds number and disk loading.

## Ceiling and wall proximity sanity

Sources: [AAU quadcopter ground/ceiling/wall thesis](https://projekter.aau.dk/projekter/files/454478098/finalquad.pdf), [Springer small-quadcopter surface-effect evaluation](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s10846-024-02155-7), [JIRS 2024 supplementary repository DOI](https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.11384638), [Robinson near-wall micro-rotorcraft CFD record](https://research.monash.edu/en/publications/computational-investigation-of-micro-rotorcraft-near-wall-hoverin/), and [Nature duct-flight surface-effect study](https://www.nature.com/articles/s44182-025-00032-5). Generated surface CSV: `docs/data/surface_proximity_effect_reference.csv`.

The ground/ceiling table scans current Java formulas at `clearance = h/R * rotor_radius`. The Cheeseman-Bennett and AAU/Kan columns are not direct fit targets; they are reference curves for the expected order of magnitude and effect range. The wall table scans the current steady lateral wall-force proxy at hover thrust.

Generated near-surface calibration packet CSV: `docs/data/surface_nearfield_calibration_packet.csv`. It condenses selected ZJU ground-effect checks, Cheeseman/AAU ground curves, current ground/ceiling rows, wall clearance mappings, wall-force scans, offline A4MC wall-skim shelter/pressure disk-gradient metrics, and published sidewall anchors into `739` narrow metrics. These rows are mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `surface_nearfield_*` categories.

Generated wall-obstruction response packet CSV: `docs/data/wall_obstruction_response_packet.csv`. It adds `1450` `wall_obstruction_packet_*` rows for formula-source inventory, flat-wall clearance response, obstruction/speed wall-force response, and compact summary metrics. The packet mirrors current `RotorFlowObstructionModel` and `DronePhysics` formulas so sidewall tuning can separate disk-overlap geometry, dirty-air thrust loss, and attraction force.

Generated A4MC source-quality response packet CSV: `docs/data/a4mc_source_quality_response_packet.csv`. It adds `17649` `a4mc_source_quality_packet_*` rows for trust, confidence, freshness, shelter, shear, source-turbulence, ABL stability/mixing, dedicated updraft/downwash sweeps, and pressure-anomaly response. The packet mirrors the current core source-quality gate and records adopted source turbulence, natural turbulence, ABL Dryden intensity/time-scale, source gust, adopted signed updraft target/settling response, terrain-shear, pressure-density/barometer/static-port response, local-voxel ventilation, hover axial-gust scaling, and duplicated-obstacle residual response proxies before those coefficients are tuned against block-edge or tunnel-mouth blackbox traces.

Generated A4MC disk-gradient response packet CSV: `docs/data/a4mc_disk_gradient_response_packet.csv`. It adds `6227` `a4mc_disk_gradient_packet_*` rows for source inventory, preset/spin/source-quality availability/raw-gradient sweeps, offline `wall_skim` pressure-gradient probes, and compact summary thresholds. The packet mirrors the current core disk-gradient response formulas for adopted gradient, tip-speed ratio, thrust loss, aerodynamic load, vibration, dynamic-stall onset, and flapping tilt before those coefficients are tuned against block-edge or tunnel-mouth blackbox traces. Runtime/offline CSV now keeps `rotor_a4mc_pressure_gradient_wind_mps` separate from `rotor_disk_wind_gradient_mps`, so pressure-driven disk loading can be audited without losing the combined gradient seen by the rotor model. `A4mcDiskGradientCalibrationTest` mirrors the packet summary in Java and reflectively compares representative responses against `DronePhysics`.

Generated A4MC local-voxel coupling packet CSV: `docs/data/a4mc_local_voxel_coupling_packet.csv`. It adds `3528` `a4mc_local_voxel_packet_*` rows for source inventory, duplicate-obstacle residual, rotor fallback, pressure-gradient, high-contrast pressure saturation, shelter-gradient, pressure-center response surfaces, and motor/ESC/battery ventilation scenarios. The pressure-center rows mirror the core availability gate for adopted asymmetric local-voxel rotor signals, including offline wall-skim, right-side wall/pressure, front wall/pressure, half-quality, and quality-zero cases. Runtime/offline CSV now also exposes `rotor_a4mc_ventilation_efficiency`, per-rotor A4MC ventilation efficiency, and `a4mc_pack_ventilation_efficiency`, so the local shelter cooling-loss path can be checked against trace rows instead of inferred from total cooling factors.

Generated partial-surface lead packet CSV: `docs/data/partial_surface_effect_lead_packet.csv`. It adds `74` `partial_surface_effect_lead_packet_*` rows from Wichita SOAR metadata for Cai/Gunasekaran/Ol's partial ground/ceiling paper. The repository item exposes the DOI and abstract but no public full-text bundle, so the packet is an area-gating/digitization lead rather than raw curve data.

Generated JIRS 2024 surface-effect packet CSV: `docs/data/surface_jirs2024_effect_packet.csv`. It adds `309` `surface_jirs2024_packet_*` rows from Springer supplementary CSV/MAT files, including normalized distance fields, same-PWM far-baseline Fz ratios for ground/ceiling, signed wall force/moment rows, and direct measurement uncertainty summaries.

Generated JIRS 2024 curve-fit packet CSV: `docs/data/surface_jirs2024_curve_fit_packet.csv`. It adds `196` `surface_jirs2024_curve_fit_*` rows: median distance bins, ground/ceiling extra-thrust exponential fits, wall force/moment distance fits split by facility, and current `racingQuad` runtime comparisons.

The packet separates three concepts that should not be collapsed into one scalar: ground/ceiling thrust multiplier, sidewall attraction/moment, and dirty-air or near-contact obstruction loss.

| Partial-surface packet item | value |
|---|---:|
| negligible plate diameter threshold | `<0.5D` |
| negligible circular patch area ratio | `<0.25` disk area |
| full-like plate diameter threshold | `1.0D` |
| reported fit accuracy | `6%` |
| `racingQuad` negligible/full-like patch diameter | `0.0635 / 0.127 m` |
| Minecraft 1 m block / `racingQuad` prop diameter | `7.87D` |

Interpretation: full Minecraft blocks are effectively infinite ground/ceiling for one 5-inch rotor, but local edges, ledges, holes, and partial-contact geometry should gate the ground/ceiling multiplier by support area. Runtime rotor-disk samples now convert supported sample coverage into an equivalent circular patch diameter and apply the packet's conservative smooth gate from `0` at `0.5D` to `1` at `1.0D`; blackbox and offline CSV traces expose the per-rotor coverage/gate values so ledge and hole passes can be audited directly. The curve is still a placeholder until the AIAA figures or tables are digitized.

For `racingQuad`, full obstruction at hover produces about `0.56 N` per rotor toward the wall in the current proxy, or roughly `0.10x` vehicle weight if two rotors are affected. This is directionally consistent with the literature's wall-attraction description, but it still needs real distance-to-wall mapping from sensor/collision geometry before it can be treated as an aerodynamic fit.

## Rain, wet prop, and water-immersion sanity

Sources: [NWS Los Angeles rain-rate visualizer](https://www.weather.gov/lox/rainrate), [Met Office rainfall measurement guide](https://www.metoffice.gov.uk/weather/guides/observations/how-we-measure-rainfall), [CIRES vapor-pressure formula summary](https://cires1.colorado.edu/~voemel/vp.html), [NIST water thermophysical data page](https://webbook.nist.gov/cgi/fluid.cgi?ID=C7732185&Action=Page), [ICAS 2020 quadrotor adverse-situations CFD](https://www.icas.org/icas_archive/ICAS2020/data/papers/ICAS2020_0482_paper.pdf), and [MDPI Drones 2022 low-altitude hovering-rotor icing tests](https://www.mdpi.com/2504-446X/6/3/68). Generated precipitation/water CSV: `docs/data/precipitation_water_effect_reference.csv`.

The rain rows convert rainfall depth rate to water mass flux with water density `997 kg/m^3`. For a concrete wetness mapping, this report treats the NWS `1.50 in/h` example (`38.100 mm/h`) as `precipitationWetness = 1`. That is an analysis convention, not a flight-test calibration.

Generated rain/water packet CSV: `docs/data/precipitation_water_packet.csv`. It condenses 1608 `precip_water_packet_*` rows into rain mass-flux scans, ICAS heavy-rain CT rows, current-vs-ICAS comparisons, moist-air-density rows, water-immersion scans, and a current Java formula audit mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv`.

Generated icing packet CSV: `docs/data/icing_rotor_mdpi_packet.csv`. It condenses 362 `icing_rotor_packet_*` rows from Villeneuve et al. into source inventory, Table 1 icing condition grid, Table 4 CT/CQ/C+Q/P+ degradation rates, endpoint projections, height/temperature/MVD ratios, and current-rain-model comparison rows mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv`.

| Rain/water packet item | value | read as |
|---|---:|---|
| rain scan rows | `42` | preset x rainfall scenario mass-flux table |
| water-immersion scan rows | `108` | preset x immersion x speed drag/thrust table |
| ICAS heavy-rain references | `2` | 4319/6528 rpm CT-loss anchors |
| racing NWS 1.50 in/h water through rotors | `0.535 g/s` | full-wetness mapping convention, not measured FPV wetness |
| racing 100 mm/h stress water through rotors | `1.403 g/s` | still tiny impact-force fraction |
| racing 100 mm/h impact/weight @8 m/s | `0.00104x` | impact momentum is not the main loss mechanism |
| ICAS equivalent rain rate | `553 mm/h` | LWC=19 g/m^3 with 8.06 m/s droplets |
| ICAS CT loss range | `1.67..2.64%` | heavy-rain CFD thrust-loss anchor |
| generated full-wet loss | `5.50%` | older wide CSV coefficient |
| current Java full-wet loss | `3.00%` | parsed from current `DronePhysics.java` |
| MDPI icing CT-loss projection | `9.13..23.96%` | icing-only, rate x published icing time |
| MDPI icing P+ endpoint projection | `20.87..89.49%` | required power increase to maintain initial thrust |
| MDPI icing/current rain loss | `3.04..7.99x` | do not merge into ordinary wetness curve |
| racing water=0.5 at 5 m/s | `49.8%` loss, `2.94x` weight drag | immersion is a separate severe exposure model |
| 35 C full-wet moist-air density | `0.979x` | humid-air density relief is small but nonzero |

| Ambient | full-wet moist-air density multiplier |
|---:|---:|
| 0 C | 0.9977x |
| 25 C | 0.9882x |
| 35 C | 0.9790x |

The calculated rain mass flux is tiny compared with rotor thrust: the NWS `1.50 in/h` example gives about `0.53 g/s` through all four `racingQuad` rotor disks, while the `100 mm/h` stress case gives about `1.40 g/s`; both have an impact-force proxy far below vehicle weight. That supports treating rain thrust loss as a wet-prop/electrical/vibration gameplay term unless real wet-prop bench data is added. By contrast, the current water-immersion path is intentionally severe: `waterImmersion = 0.5` already removes about half of rotor thrust and adds large body drag.

The MDPI icing source is intentionally separate from the ordinary rain model. Its Table 4 cases use a 0.66 m, four-blade Bell APT70-style rotor in hover at `4950 rpm`, `11.7 deg`, `lambda=80 g/dm^2/h`, and `MVD=120/800 um`. Published linear slopes give CT decline rates of `0.012..0.226%/s`, CQ rise rates of `0.047..0.565%/s`, and stopping times of `106..761 s`. Use those rows only for a future frozen-contamination state with temperature/exposure-time gates and shedding/de-icing logic.

## Motor and inflow response sanity

RotorS Firefly/Hummingbird and PX4 Iris use first-order motor lag values of `timeConstantUp = 0.0125 s` and `timeConstantDown = 0.0250 s`. This project's `motor_tau` likely includes more than a bare motor command lag, while `rotor_inflow_tau` is an aerodynamic wake term. Generated inflow time-scale CSV: `docs/data/rotor_inflow_time_scale_reference.csv`.

The inflow proxy uses hover momentum theory `vi = sqrt(T/(2 rho A))`; `R/vi` and `2R/vi` are wake-transit scales, not a complete Pitt-Peters or finite-state dynamic-inflow fit.

| Preset | motor tau | inflow tau | R/vi | 2R/vi | tau/(R/vi) | tau/(2R/vi) | lag coeff | motor/up ref |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | 0.0450 s | 0.0350 s | 0.0068 s | 0.0136 s | 5.14x | 2.57x | 0.16 | 3.60x |
| cinewhoop | 0.0700 s | 0.0550 s | 0.0026 s | 0.0053 s | 20.95x | 10.48x | 0.20 | 5.60x |
| heavyLift | 0.1200 s | 0.0950 s | 0.0135 s | 0.0269 s | 7.05x | 3.53x | 0.18 | 9.60x |
| hexLift | 0.0950 s | 0.0850 s | 0.0117 s | 0.0233 s | 7.28x | 3.64x | 0.17 | 7.60x |
| octoLift | 0.1050 s | 0.0900 s | 0.0127 s | 0.0254 s | 7.08x | 3.54x | 0.18 | 8.40x |
| coaxialX8 | 0.1050 s | 0.0900 s | 0.0124 s | 0.0247 s | 7.29x | 3.64x | 0.18 | 8.40x |

## ESC electrical headroom, braking, and desync sanity

Sources: [Betaflight DShot API](https://betaflight.com/docs/development/API/Dshot), [Betaflight DShot RPM filtering](https://betaflight.com/docs/wiki/guides/current/DSHOT-RPM-Filtering), [Bluejay ESC firmware README](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/bird-sanctuary/bluejay/master/README.md), [AM32 ESC firmware README](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/am32-firmware/AM32/main/README.md), and [TI sensorless trapezoidal BLDC/BEMF application report](https://www.ti.com/lit/pdf/sprabq7). Generated ESC electrical CSV: `docs/data/esc_electrical_dynamics_reference.csv`.

This table mirrors the current Java model's inferred motor-electrical scale: `maxOmega * MOTOR_NO_LOAD_OMEGA_SCALE / nominalVoltage` for KV, `Kt = 1 / KV(rad/s/V)`, and `R = V / (perMotorCurrentLimit * MOTOR_STALL_CURRENT_SCALE)` for a winding-resistance proxy. The power-current columns use `shaft_power / (V * 0.75)` as a DC battery-current sanity check; the phase-current proxy is not a battery-current estimate.

| Preset | inferred KV | Kt | winding R | headroom hover/max | shaft current hover/max | max current/limit | braking current/torque @max | brake tau | full slew up/down |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | 2341 rpm/V | 0.0041 N*m/A | 0.233 ohm | 0.669/0.259 | 4.087/45.769 A | 2.03x | 29.333 A / 0.120 N*m | 14.062 ms | 6.250/2.778 ms |
| cinewhoop | 727 rpm/V | 0.0131 N*m/A | 0.285 ohm | 0.600/0.259 | 1.228/7.815 A | 0.48x | 14.637 A / 0.192 N*m | 27.778 ms | 12.500/6.667 ms |
| heavyLift | 534 rpm/V | 0.0179 N*m/A | 0.198 ohm | 0.601/0.259 | 9.843/62.918 A | 1.80x | 20.741 A / 0.371 N*m | 60.000 ms | 22.222/14.286 ms |
| hexLift | 494 rpm/V | 0.0194 N*m/A | 0.260 ohm | 0.619/0.259 | 4.321/31.850 A | 1.19x | 18.963 A / 0.367 N*m | 43.182 ms | 18.182/11.111 ms |
| octoLift | 377 rpm/V | 0.0253 N*m/A | 0.336 ohm | 0.563/0.259 | 4.408/21.534 A | 0.78x | 18.252 A / 0.462 N*m | 49.528 ms | 20.000/11.765 ms |
| coaxialX8 | 377 rpm/V | 0.0253 N*m/A | 0.336 ohm | 0.551/0.259 | 4.802/21.534 A | 0.78x | 18.252 A / 0.462 N*m | 49.528 ms | 20.000/11.765 ms |

| Reference | Protocol / feature | Key values | Source |
|---|---|---:|---|
| Betaflight DShot300 raw frame | protocol_reference | 53.333 us raw frame, 2000 throttle steps | [source](https://betaflight.com/docs/development/API/Dshot) |
| Betaflight DShot600 raw frame | protocol_reference | 26.667 us raw frame, 2000 throttle steps | [source](https://betaflight.com/docs/development/API/Dshot) |
| Bluejay ESC firmware features | firmware_reference | DShot300/600, bidirectional DShot, PWM 24-96 kHz | [source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/bird-sanctuary/bluejay/master/README.md) |
| AM32 ESC firmware features | firmware_reference | DShot300/600, bidirectional DShot, ESC telemetry, variable PWM, sinusoidal startup | [source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/am32-firmware/AM32/main/README.md) |
| TI SPRABQ7 sensorless trapezoidal BLDC BEMF | motor_control_reference | Sensorless BLDC six-step/back-EMF commutation background | [source](https://www.ti.com/lit/pdf/sprabq7) |

The important model check is headroom and current scale. For `racingQuad`, the configured max-thrust point is close to the inferred no-load voltage ceiling and above the per-motor battery-current budget under a simple shaft-power estimate. That does not prove the runtime can never hit the configured thrust, because the real ESC/battery/current model has transients and limits, but it is a clear flag that max-thrust, current-limit, and voltage-headroom claims should be tested together.

## Rotor inertia and gyroscopic torque sanity

Sources: [RotorS Firefly](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ethz-asl/rotors_simulator/master/rotors_description/urdf/firefly.xacro), [RotorS Hummingbird](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ethz-asl/rotors_simulator/master/rotors_description/urdf/hummingbird.xacro), [ZJU ground-effect/motor-calibration supplement](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ZJU-FAST-Lab/Ground-effect-controller/master/README.md), official HQProp prop pages, and official Gemfan prop pages. Generated rotor-inertia CSV: `docs/data/rotor_inertia_gyro_reference.csv`.

The equivalent-mass columns use `I = c * m * R^2`: `c=1/3` is a uniform slender-blade proxy, `c=0.25` is hub-biased, `c=0.5` is tip-biased, and `c=1.0` is a ring upper bound. Gyro torque uses per-rotor angular momentum `H = I * omega` at a body rate of `720` deg/s. Opposite spin directions cancel in ideal symmetric hover, so the all-rotors column is an absolute disturbance bound, not a net hover torque.

| Preset | radius | Irotor | eq mass c=1/3 | hover/max RPM | H hover/max | gyro per rotor @max | spin-up torque tau/50ms |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | 0.0635 m | 5.376e-06 kg*m^2 | 4.000 g | 13023/29138 | 0.007/0.016 N*m*s | 0.206 N*m | 0.365/0.328 N*m |
| cinewhoop | 0.0380 m | 9.000e-06 kg*m^2 | 18.698 g | 4297/7965 | 0.004/0.008 N*m*s | 0.094 N*m | 0.107/0.150 N*m |
| heavyLift | 0.1270 m | 8.500e-05 kg*m^2 | 15.810 g | 4728/8775 | 0.042/0.078 N*m*s | 0.982 N*m | 0.651/1.562 N*m |
| hexLift | 0.1050 m | 6.200e-05 kg*m^2 | 16.871 g | 4170/8115 | 0.027/0.053 N*m*s | 0.662 N*m | 0.555/1.054 N*m |
| octoLift | 0.1150 m | 7.000e-05 kg*m^2 | 15.879 g | 4874/8270 | 0.036/0.061 N*m*s | 0.762 N*m | 0.577/1.212 N*m |
| coaxialX8 | 0.1150 m | 7.000e-05 kg*m^2 | 15.879 g | 5015/8270 | 0.037/0.061 N*m*s | 0.762 N*m | 0.577/1.212 N*m |

| Reference | radius | rotor mass | Irotor | eq mass c=1/3 | eq mass ring | note |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| [source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ethz-asl/rotors_simulator/master/rotors_description/urdf/firefly.xacro): RotorS Firefly physical rotor mass | 0.1000 m | 5.000 g | 4.260e-06 kg*m^2 | 1.278 g | 0.426 g | RotorS cuboid rotor inertia; sim row multiplies rotor mass by rotor_velocity_slowdown_sim. |
| [source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ethz-asl/rotors_simulator/master/rotors_description/urdf/firefly.xacro): RotorS Firefly sim slowdown mass | 0.1000 m | 50.000 g | 4.260e-05 kg*m^2 | 12.781 g | 4.260 g | RotorS cuboid rotor inertia; sim row multiplies rotor mass by rotor_velocity_slowdown_sim. |
| [source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ethz-asl/rotors_simulator/master/rotors_description/urdf/hummingbird.xacro): RotorS Hummingbird physical rotor mass | 0.1000 m | 9.000 g | 7.669e-06 kg*m^2 | 2.301 g | 0.767 g | RotorS cuboid rotor inertia; sim row multiplies rotor mass by rotor_velocity_slowdown_sim. |
| [source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ethz-asl/rotors_simulator/master/rotors_description/urdf/hummingbird.xacro): RotorS Hummingbird sim slowdown mass | 0.1000 m | 90.000 g | 7.669e-05 kg*m^2 | 23.006 g | 7.669 g | RotorS cuboid rotor inertia; sim row multiplies rotor mass by rotor_velocity_slowdown_sim. |
| [source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ZJU-FAST-Lab/Ground-effect-controller/master/README.md): ZJU reported rotor inertia JR | 0.0889 m | 7.500 g | 1.056e-04 kg*m^2 | 40.070 g | 13.357 g | Source-reported JR with 7-inch 7.5g paddle BOM; source table writes rpm-based coefficients, so treat as an identified inertia scale before direct SI transplant. |

| coaxialX8 vs [Gemfan 1050 Cinelifter glass-fiber nylon 3-blade](https://www.gemfanhobby.com/1050-cinelifter-glass-fiber-nylon-3-blade.html) | 10.4% | 16.800 g | 1.03x | 0.78x | 0.52x | 0.95x |

RotorS' physical Hummingbird cuboid inertia is `7.669e-06` kg*m^2, while its simulation-slowdown row is 10x larger because the xacro multiplies rotor mass by `rotor_velocity_slowdown_sim`. ZJU reports `JR=1.056e-04` for a 7-inch platform; because that source identifies thrust/torque with RPM-based coefficients, keep it as a scale/reference row until the unit convention is checked against the original dynamic fit.
Physical prop mass rows sharpen the interpretation: `racingQuad` is below 5-inch prop-only uniform inertia (`0.88..1.05x`), while `cinewhoop` is far above 3-inch/D90 prop-only inertia (`5.8..12.6x`). The `heavyLift` 10-inch preset is closer to official 10-inch tri-blade masses at `0.89..0.94x` the uniform estimate.

## Rotor arm flex and blade coning sanity

Sources: [FAA Helicopter Flying Handbook coning background](https://www.faa.gov/sites/faa.gov/files/regulations_policies/handbooks_manuals/aviation/helicopter_flying_handbook/hfh_ch02.pdf), [NASA multicopter blade-deflection study](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf), [NASA cantilever deflection note](https://ntrs.nasa.gov/api/citations/19690026842/downloads/19690026842.pdf), [NASA cantilever tip-mass frequency note](https://ntrs.nasa.gov/api/citations/19760006440/downloads/19760006440.pdf), and [ACP carbon-fiber composite properties](https://acpcomposites.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/12/Mechanical-Properties-of-Carbon-Fiber-Composite-Materials.pdf). Generated arm-flex/coning CSV: `docs/data/rotor_arm_flex_coning_reference.csv`.

The Java `rotorConingIntensity` is a normalized load/vibration/thrust-loss proxy, not a literal blade coning angle. The NASA blade rows below are therefore magnitude anchors for prop elastic deflection, while the arm rows compare the separate frame-arm flex proxy against first-order cantilever beam scales.

| NASA multicopter prop measurement | method | RPM | deflection | coning angle |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| [T-motor 15x5](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf) | DSLR camera | 2000 | 0.220 mm | 0.11 deg |
| [T-motor 15x5](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf) | DSLR camera | 3500 | 1.440 mm | 0.69 deg |
| [T-motor 15x5](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf) | DSLR camera | 5000 | 1.870 mm | 0.89 deg |
| [T-motor 15x5](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf) | photogrammetry | 5000 | 1.120 mm |  |
| [DJI Phantom 3](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf) | DSLR camera mean | 3000 | 1.060 mm | 0.51 deg |
| [DJI Phantom 3](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf) | DSLR camera mean | 5000 | 2.470 mm | 1.18 deg |
| [DJI Phantom 3](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf) | DSLR camera mean | 7500 | 3.730 mm | 1.78 deg |
| [DJI Phantom 3](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Nowicki_CR-2017-219428_Final.pdf) | DSLR camera mean | 8500 | 4.080 mm | 1.95 deg |

For `racingQuad`, full flex would be about `9.9 mm` at the rotor tip, but the steady max-load target is only `0.16` and the max-snap proxy is `0.60`, so the generated deflection rows are more useful than the full-flex cap alone. The 6x4 mm carbon-arm sensitivity case lands near the current max-snap deflection, while the 10x5 mm case is much stiffer; real calibration needs actual arm section, laminate direction, motor mass, and frame joint stiffness.

## Contact, collision, and prop-strike data packet

Sources: [Engineering ToolBox friction table](https://www.engineeringtoolbox.com/friction-coefficients-d_778.html), [Physics Factbook restitution table](https://hypertextbook.com/facts/2006/restitution.shtml), [RocFall restitution background](https://www.rocscience.com/help/rocfall/documentation/slope/materials/coefficient-of-restitution), [RocFall thesis default ranges](https://static.rocscience.cloud/assets/verification-and-theory/RocFall/thesis_body.pdf), [UAV Realistic Fault Dataset](https://github.com/tiiuae/UAV-Realistic-Fault-Dataset) and [ICRA 2023 paper](https://secplab.ppgia.pucpr.br/files/papers/2023icra.pdf), [DJI Mini 2 propeller damage vibration dataset](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41597-025-05692-4), and [PADRE UAV propeller-fault measurement data](https://github.com/AeroLabPUT/UAV_measurement_data). Generated contact CSV: `docs/data/contact_collision_reference.csv`. Generated raw vibration summary CSV: `docs/data/propeller_damage_vibration_reference.csv`.

The CSV keeps the public material/contact values separate from current-code mirrors. For the current-code rows, `vertical_restitution_code` and `horizontal_restitution_code` are effective bounce multipliers from `ContactDynamics`, while friction rows report velocity-retention proxies rather than literal material friction coefficients.

Generated propeller-damage/vibration packet CSV: `docs/data/propeller_damage_vibration_packet.csv`. It condenses 469 `prop_damage_packet_*` rows into UAV Realistic fault aggregates, DJI Mini 2 raw vibration spectra, PADRE FFT feature ratios, current rotor-damage scan rows, and blade-pass alias checks mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv`. The supplemental DronePropB packets add `docs/data/dronepropb_sample_packet.csv` with 1195 `dronepropb_sample_packet_*` rows for full file inventory and a 12-file C3 sample, plus `docs/data/dronepropb_stratified_vibration_packet.csv` with 774 `dronepropb_stratified_packet_*` rows for speed/channel/severity stratification.

| Prop-damage packet item | value | read as |
|---|---:|---|
| UAV Realistic SensorCombined files | `99` | flight-phase-inclusive JSONL missions |
| UAV Realistic class count | `5` | 0-4 broken-propeller labels |
| strongest SensorCombined gyro ratio | `2.34x`, class `4` | fault/noise envelope, not steady hover |
| strongest SensorCombined accel ratio | `7.41x`, class `4` | largest sampled acceleration separation |
| strongest raw-IMU accel ratio | `1.52x`, class `3` | local frame-id amplitude evidence |
| strongest AudioBuffer payload RMS ratio | `1.03x`, class `4` | raw payload amplitude weakly separated |
| DronePropB file inventory | `111` `.mat`, `570.5 MB` by file tree | full source tree recorded, not fully mirrored |
| DronePropB selected C3 samples | `12` files | healthy speeds plus F1-F3/SV1-SV3 at SP2 |
| DronePropB healthy SP3 / SP2 RMS | `3.30x` | speed effect can dominate damage amplitude |
| DronePropB selected SP2 fault RMS ratio | median/max `1.20x/1.49x` | ground-test C3 subset versus healthy SP2 |
| DronePropB stratified selected files | `26` files, `88.1 MB` cached | targeted speed/channel/severity subset |
| DronePropB same-baseline fault rows | `21` | each compared against healthy same speed/channel |
| DronePropB stratified fault RMS ratio | median/P90/max `1.184x/1.488x/2.246x` | normalized external-accelerometer feature scale |
| DronePropB strongest selected row | `F3_SV2_SP3_C3.mat` | high-speed C3 case, not generic scalar |
| DronePropB fixed SV2/SP2 channel medians | C1/C2/C3 `1.147x/1.034x/1.320x` | placement/channel effect remains visible |
| DJI sample / Nyquist | `1024/512 Hz` | cannot directly observe FPV hover BPF |
| DJI healthy dominant peak | `159.678 Hz` | two-blade Mini 2 vibration peak |
| DJI vector RMS ratio range | `0.96..1.15x` | raw RMS is not monotonic enough alone |
| racingQuad hover/max BPF | `651/1457 Hz` | true current three-blade blade-pass |
| racingQuad BPF aliases in DJI data | `372/433 Hz` | alias bookkeeping, not direct notch targets |
| PADRE strongest FFT label | `2010`, `3.13x` | normalized feature separation, not m/s^2 |
| current damage vibration range | `0..0.75` | dimensionless runtime intensity scan |

| DJI Mini 2 accelerometer propeller damage dataset | healthy, bottom-right damaged, bottom-right unbalanced, top-right damaged, top-right unbalanced | dataset/log labels | [source](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41597-025-05692-4) |

UAV Realistic Fault Dataset inventory: `99` SensorCombined missions, `9` raw Imu files, and `99` AudioBuffer files across five classes, with `3475` MB of JSONL files by GitHub tree metadata. Bandwidth note: the dataset sample rate is `1024` Hz (`Nyquist 512 Hz`). The current `racingQuad` configured hover/max blade-pass frequencies are `651.155/1457` Hz, so this dataset is useful for fault-vibration feature scale but cannot directly resolve the current 3-blade FPV hover/max blade-pass without aliasing.

The raw DJI Mini 2 fault cases do not map monotonically to one scalar vibration amplitude: the strongest vector-RMS case is only modestly above healthy, while spectral distribution and rotor location carry important information. PADRE's sampled FFT subset adds a clearer multi-x feature-RMS separation for labeled actuator faults, but those rows are normalized features rather than physical acceleration. Treat the current damage-vibration scalar as a gameplay/diagnostic intensity until calibrated against a vehicle-specific sensor placement and prop/motor speed.

## Motor, ESC, and winding thermal sanity

Sources: [U8/Kv100 processed dyno data](https://github.com/thhsieh/U8-Kv100-Dyno-Data), [Mini Quad Test Bench Emax Eco 2306 2400kv](https://www.miniquadtestbench.com/assets/components/motordata/motorinfo.php?uid=259), [copper temperature-coefficient reference](https://www.copper.org/publications/newsletters/innovations/2001/08/intro_fac.html), [motor insulation-class context](https://www.theaemt.com/resource/insulation-classes-for-electric-motors.html), and [Infineon IRL40SC228 MOSFET page](https://www.infineon.com/part/IRL40SC228). Generated thermal CSV: `docs/data/motor_esc_thermal_reference.csv`.

The U8/Kv100 data is a larger motor/driver dyno map, not an FPV 2306 motor. The MQTB row is a direct FPV-class motor/test-stand metadata anchor, but it does not report winding or ESC temperature rise. The current-preset table mirrors this project's thermal equations using sea-level density and no obstruction/recirculation; steady rises are model proxies, not lab measurements.

Generated thermal packet CSV: `docs/data/motor_thermal_packet.csv`. It reshapes the U8 dyno rows, MQTB FPV metadata, current thermal limits, current electrical stress, and copper resistance scaling into 240 narrow metrics, mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `motor_thermal_packet_*` categories.

| Motor thermal packet item | value | read as |
|---|---:|---|
| U8 36 V open-dyno max temperature | `57.69` C | cross-class BLDC thermal/loss anchor |
| U8 36 V open-dyno max loss | `484.17` W | high-load loss scale, not FPV 2306 coefficient |
| MQTB Emax Eco 2306 tested KV | `2300 rpm/V` | FPV hardware-class anchor |
| `racingQuad` inferred KV / MQTB tested KV | `1.018x` | electrical class is FPV-plausible |
| `racingQuad` per-motor limit / MQTB ESC rating | `0.5625x` | configured current limit is below that test ESC rating |
| `racingQuad` full-power motor temp at 25 C ambient | `203.6` C | model predicts thermal limiting under sustained full power |
| `racingQuad` full-power motor rise / cutoff margin | `1.79x` | current proxy exceeds cutoff margin |
| `racingQuad` full-power ESC temp at 25 C ambient | `117.6` C | proxy sits just below `120 C` ESC cutoff |

| U8 map | voltage | max temp | loss mean/max | motor eff max | driver eff max | rpm max | torque max | current max | max-temp point current/rpm/torque |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| U8_Kv100_24V | 24 V | 48.623 C | 116.262/406.677 W | 0.659 | 0.974 | 1505 | 3.173 N*m | 50.000 A | 50.000 A / 901 rpm / 1.465 N*m |
| U8_Kv100_36V | 36 V | 57.692 C | 132.231/484.167 W | 0.682 | 0.980 | 1704 | 3.379 N*m | 50.000 A | 50.000 A / 0 rpm / 3.379 N*m |

The MQTB 2306 row supports the current racing preset's FPV motor KV/current class, while the U8 map and copper coefficient support broad BLDC loss/temperature direction. The exact thermal rise/cooling constants remain gameplay/model coefficients until matched to FPV motor temperature telemetry or a 2306/2806 bench with thermocouple/IR measurements.

## RPM, filtering, and command timing sanity

References: [Betaflight DShot/RPM filtering](https://betaflight.com/docs/wiki/guides/current/DSHOT-RPM-Filtering), [Betaflight PID/filter tuning](https://betaflight.com/docs/wiki/guides/current/PID-Tuning-Guide), and [ExpressLRS packet-rate context](https://www.expresslrs.org/software/switch-config/). Betaflight-style RPM filtering is normally motor-RPM telemetry aware; this project's current gyro vibration telemetry uses an average motor notch plus a blade-pass notch derived from each preset's `RotorSpec.bladeCount`.

| Preset | blades | hover RPM | max RPM | configured blade-pass hover/max | 3-blade hover/max | gyro LPF | RC frame | ESC frame | latency/smoothing |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | 3 | 13023 | 29138 | 651/1457 Hz | 651/1457 Hz | 120 Hz | 150 Hz / 6.667 ms | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | control 15.000 ms, RC 18.000 ms, smooth 18.000 ms |
| cinewhoop | 3 | 4297 | 7965 | 215/398 Hz | 215/398 Hz | 90 Hz | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | control 18.000 ms, RC 25.000 ms, smooth 25.000 ms |
| heavyLift | 2 | 4728 | 8775 | 158/293 Hz | 236/439 Hz | 70 Hz | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | control 25.000 ms, RC 35.000 ms, smooth 40.000 ms |
| hexLift | 2 | 4170 | 8115 | 139/271 Hz | 208/406 Hz | 75 Hz | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | control 22.000 ms, RC 35.000 ms, smooth 40.000 ms |
| octoLift | 2 | 4874 | 8270 | 162/276 Hz | 244/413 Hz | 70 Hz | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | control 24.000 ms, RC 40.000 ms, smooth 45.000 ms |
| coaxialX8 | 2 | 5015 | 8270 | 167/276 Hz | 251/413 Hz | 70 Hz | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | control 24.000 ms, RC 40.000 ms, smooth 45.000 ms |

For 5-inch FPV three-blade props, `racingQuad` and `cinewhoop` now use a physical three-blade blade-pass frequency. Keep `RotorSpec.bladeCount` aligned with the prop family used for each preset, especially before using blackbox RPM spectra for validation.

### RC, ESC, and log-rate protocol anchors

References: [ExpressLRS switch/channel resolution](https://www.expresslrs.org/software/switch-config/), [ExpressLRS Lua packet-rate notes](https://www.expresslrs.org/quick-start/transmitters/lua-howto/), [ExpressLRS RF-mode table](https://www.expresslrs.org/info/signal-health/), [Betaflight DShot API](https://betaflight.com/docs/development/API/Dshot), and [Betaflight blackbox guide](https://betaflight.com/docs/wiki/guides/current/Black-Box-logging-and-usage). Generated RC/ESC timing CSV: `docs/data/rc_esc_timing_reference.csv`.

The reference rows separate protocol packet/frame timing from true end-to-end latency. ExpressLRS packet rate is not the same thing as stick-to-motor delay, and raw DShot frame time is not the same thing as ESC motor update cadence, but both are useful bounds for spotting slow or overly quantized simulation settings.

| Preset | RC rate/interval | nearest ELRS | RC step | RC latency/smoothing frames | ESC rate/interval | ESC step | ESC interval vs raw DShot300/DShot600 |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | 150 Hz / 6.667 ms | 150 Hz | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 2.70 / 2.70 frames | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 46.9x / 93.8x |
| cinewhoop | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 100 Hz | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 2.50 / 2.50 frames | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 46.9x / 93.8x |
| heavyLift | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 100 Hz | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 3.50 / 4.00 frames | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 46.9x / 93.8x |
| hexLift | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 100 Hz | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 3.50 / 4.00 frames | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 46.9x / 93.8x |
| octoLift | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 100 Hz | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 4.00 / 4.50 frames | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 46.9x / 93.8x |
| coaxialX8 | 100 Hz / 10.000 ms | 100 Hz | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 4.00 / 4.50 frames | 400 Hz / 2.500 ms | 2048 steps / 0.049% | 46.9x / 93.8x |

The current `racingQuad` RC rate of 150 Hz lines up with an ELRS packet-rate anchor, but its 18 ms RC latency and 18 ms smoothing each span about 2.7 configured RC frames. Its 400 Hz ESC command frame is much slower than raw DShot frame capacity, which is plausible as a simplified motor-command model but should not be described as literal DShot timing.

### Rate curve and stick mapping sanity

References: [Betaflight Rate Calculator](https://betaflight.com/docs/wiki/guides/current/Rate-Calculator), [Betaflight `rc.c` rate formulas](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/betaflight/betaflight/master/src/main/fc/rc.c), and [Betaflight Configurator RateCurve.js](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/betaflight/betaflight-configurator/master/src/js/RateCurve.js). Generated control-rate CSV: `docs/data/control_rate_reference.csv`.

The project formula uses `shapeRateInput(stick, expo, superRate) * maxRate`. Unlike Betaflight's older rate model, the current project `superRate` does not raise full-stick max rate; it softens center/mid-stick authority while preserving the configured `maxRate` at full stick. The Betaflight Actual comparison below uses the same full rate and center slope so the shape difference is visible without pretending the UI parameters are interchangeable.

| Preset axis | max rate | center sensitivity | half-stick rate | 0.75-stick rate | Betaflight band |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| racingQuad yaw | 520 deg/s | 354 deg/s/stick | 203 deg/s | 339 deg/s | outside race/freestyle guide |
| racingQuad roll | 720 deg/s | 257 deg/s/stick | 175 deg/s | 352 deg/s | outside race/freestyle guide |
| cinewhoop yaw | 320 deg/s | 211 deg/s/stick | 120 deg/s | 204 deg/s | outside race/freestyle guide |
| cinewhoop roll | 430 deg/s | 177 deg/s/stick | 116 deg/s | 229 deg/s | outside race/freestyle guide |
| heavyLift yaw | 180 deg/s | 132 deg/s/stick | 73 deg/s | 120 deg/s | outside race/freestyle guide |
| heavyLift roll | 260 deg/s | 155 deg/s/stick | 91 deg/s | 160 deg/s | outside race/freestyle guide |

| racingQuad roll stick | current target | Betaflight Actual same full+center | delta |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 0.25 | 72.0 deg/s | 83.2 deg/s | -11.2 deg/s |
| 0.50 | 175.1 deg/s | 206.4 deg/s | -31.3 deg/s |
| 0.75 | 352.2 deg/s | 391.0 deg/s | -38.8 deg/s |
| 1.00 | 720.0 deg/s | 720.0 deg/s | 0.0 deg/s |

For `racingQuad`, roll/pitch at `720 deg/s` is faster than Betaflight's common race guide but not in the common freestyle range; yaw at `520 deg/s` sits just below the race guide. This supports the current preset as a quick racing-style tune with relatively soft center roll/pitch authority, not a literal Betaflight profile import.

## IMU noise and LPF sanity

Sources: [MPU-6000/6050 datasheet](https://www.cdiweb.com/datasheets/invensense/mpu-6050_datasheet_v3%204.pdf), [ICM-20602 product page](https://bluerobotics.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/05/ICM20602-DATASHEET.pdf), [BMI270 datasheet](https://www.bosch-sensortec.com/media/boschsensortec/downloads/datasheets/bst-bmi270-ds000.pdf), and [ICM-42688-P product page](https://invensense.tdk.com/en-us/products/6-axis/icm-42688-p). The generated IMU CSV is `docs/data/imu_noise_reference_summary.csv`.

The calculation treats datasheet noise density as white noise and estimates RMS after a one-pole low-pass with `ENBW = pi/2 * cutoff`. This is a sanity check for electronics noise scale; real FPV gyro noise also includes frame resonance, motor/prop vibration, aliasing, mounting, and filter topology.

| Preset | sensor | gyro LPF | gyro RMS ref | configured gyro | gyro ratio | accel LPF | accel RMS ref | configured accel | accel ratio |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | [MPU-6000/MPU-6050](https://www.cdiweb.com/datasheets/invensense/mpu-6050_datasheet_v3%204.pdf) | 120 Hz | 0.001 rad/s | 0.025 rad/s | 20.9x | 80 Hz | 0.044 m/s^2 | 0.220 m/s^2 | 5.0x |
| racingQuad | [ICM-42688-P](https://invensense.tdk.com/en-us/products/6-axis/icm-42688-p) | 120 Hz | 6.709e-04 rad/s | 0.025 rad/s | 37.3x | 80 Hz | 0.008 m/s^2 | 0.220 m/s^2 | 28.6x |
| cinewhoop | [MPU-6000/MPU-6050](https://www.cdiweb.com/datasheets/invensense/mpu-6050_datasheet_v3%204.pdf) | 90 Hz | 0.001 rad/s | 0.018 rad/s | 17.3x | 65 Hz | 0.040 m/s^2 | 0.200 m/s^2 | 5.0x |
| cinewhoop | [ICM-42688-P](https://invensense.tdk.com/en-us/products/6-axis/icm-42688-p) | 90 Hz | 5.811e-04 rad/s | 0.018 rad/s | 31.0x | 65 Hz | 0.007 m/s^2 | 0.200 m/s^2 | 28.8x |
| heavyLift | [MPU-6000/MPU-6050](https://www.cdiweb.com/datasheets/invensense/mpu-6050_datasheet_v3%204.pdf) | 70 Hz | 9.151e-04 rad/s | 0.012 rad/s | 13.1x | 45 Hz | 0.033 m/s^2 | 0.160 m/s^2 | 4.9x |
| heavyLift | [ICM-42688-P](https://invensense.tdk.com/en-us/products/6-axis/icm-42688-p) | 70 Hz | 5.124e-04 rad/s | 0.012 rad/s | 23.4x | 45 Hz | 0.006 m/s^2 | 0.160 m/s^2 | 27.7x |
| hexLift | [MPU-6000/MPU-6050](https://www.cdiweb.com/datasheets/invensense/mpu-6050_datasheet_v3%204.pdf) | 75 Hz | 9.472e-04 rad/s | 0.014 rad/s | 14.8x | 42 Hz | 0.032 m/s^2 | 0.140 m/s^2 | 4.4x |
| hexLift | [ICM-42688-P](https://invensense.tdk.com/en-us/products/6-axis/icm-42688-p) | 75 Hz | 5.304e-04 rad/s | 0.014 rad/s | 26.4x | 42 Hz | 0.006 m/s^2 | 0.140 m/s^2 | 25.1x |
| octoLift | [MPU-6000/MPU-6050](https://www.cdiweb.com/datasheets/invensense/mpu-6050_datasheet_v3%204.pdf) | 70 Hz | 9.151e-04 rad/s | 0.014 rad/s | 15.3x | 38 Hz | 0.030 m/s^2 | 0.140 m/s^2 | 4.6x |
| octoLift | [ICM-42688-P](https://invensense.tdk.com/en-us/products/6-axis/icm-42688-p) | 70 Hz | 5.124e-04 rad/s | 0.014 rad/s | 27.3x | 38 Hz | 0.005 m/s^2 | 0.140 m/s^2 | 26.4x |
| coaxialX8 | [MPU-6000/MPU-6050](https://www.cdiweb.com/datasheets/invensense/mpu-6050_datasheet_v3%204.pdf) | 70 Hz | 9.151e-04 rad/s | 0.014 rad/s | 15.3x | 38 Hz | 0.030 m/s^2 | 0.140 m/s^2 | 4.6x |
| coaxialX8 | [ICM-42688-P](https://invensense.tdk.com/en-us/products/6-axis/icm-42688-p) | 70 Hz | 5.124e-04 rad/s | 0.014 rad/s | 27.3x | 38 Hz | 0.005 m/s^2 | 0.140 m/s^2 | 26.4x |

The current sensor-noise values are consistently several times to tens of times above bare IMU electronics noise. That can be reasonable for a gameplay/FPV feel model if these parameters intentionally represent residual vibration after filtering; if they are meant as electronics-only noise, they are high.

## Barometer pressure and altitude sanity

Sources: [BMP280 datasheet](https://www.bosch-sensortec.com/media/boschsensortec/downloads/datasheets/bst-bmp280-ds001.pdf), [BMP388 datasheet](https://www.bosch-sensortec.com/media/boschsensortec/downloads/datasheets/bst-bmp388-ds001.pdf), [DPS310 datasheet](https://www.infineon.com/dgdl/Infineon-DPS310-DataSheet-v01_02-EN.pdf?fileId=5546d462576f34750157750826c42242), [MS5611 datasheet](https://www.hpinfotech.ro/MS5611-01BA03.pdf), and [NASA dynamic pressure/atmosphere context](https://www.grc.nasa.gov/www/k-12/airplane/atmosmet.html). Generated barometer CSV: `docs/data/barometer_reference_summary.csv`.

Near sea level, `1 Pa` pressure error is about `0.083 m` altitude error by `dh = dp / (rho g)`. The table separates sensor pressure noise from the project's simulated pressure-port/propwash/dynamic-pressure error.

| Sensor | pressure noise | altitude noise | relative accuracy | relative altitude | note |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| [Bosch BMP280](https://www.bosch-sensortec.com/media/boschsensortec/downloads/datasheets/bst-bmp280-ds001.pdf) | 1.300 Pa | 0.1082 m | 12.000 Pa | 0.999 m | RMS pressure noise typical at ultra-high-resolution setting; relative accuracy from datasheet operating range. |
| [Bosch BMP388](https://www.bosch-sensortec.com/media/boschsensortec/downloads/datasheets/bst-bmp388-ds001.pdf) | 0.640 Pa | 0.0533 m | 8.000 Pa | 0.666 m | Datasheet pressure noise/relative accuracy used as sensor-only floor. |
| [Infineon DPS310](https://www.infineon.com/dgdl/Infineon-DPS310-DataSheet-v01_02-EN.pdf?fileId=5546d462576f34750157750826c42242) | 0.200 Pa | 0.0166 m | 6.000 Pa | 0.499 m | High-precision pressure mode; relative accuracy used for slow altitude bias floor. |
| [TE MS5611-01BA03](https://www.hpinfotech.ro/MS5611-01BA03.pdf) | 1.200 Pa | 0.0999 m | 10.000 Pa | 0.832 m | 0.012 mbar pressure resolution converted to Pa; relative accuracy is approximate absolute/temperature residual scale. |

| Preset | accel noise | quiet baro amplitude | quiet baro RMS | altitude tau | vertical-speed tau |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | 0.220 m/s^2 | 0.0077 m | 0.0059 m | 0.090 s | 0.180 s |
| cinewhoop | 0.200 m/s^2 | 0.0070 m | 0.0053 m | 0.090 s | 0.180 s |
| heavyLift | 0.160 m/s^2 | 0.0056 m | 0.0043 m | 0.090 s | 0.180 s |
| hexLift | 0.140 m/s^2 | 0.0049 m | 0.0037 m | 0.090 s | 0.180 s |
| octoLift | 0.140 m/s^2 | 0.0049 m | 0.0037 m | 0.090 s | 0.180 s |
| coaxialX8 | 0.140 m/s^2 | 0.0049 m | 0.0037 m | 0.090 s | 0.180 s |

| Airspeed | flow mode | dynamic pressure head | code altitude error | equivalent pressure coefficient |
|---:|---|---:|---:|---:|
| 5 m/s | aligned | 1.275 m | -5.796e-04 m | -4.547e-04 |
| 5 m/s | broadside_separated | 1.275 m | 4.012e-04 m | 3.148e-04 |
| 10 m/s | aligned | 5.099 m | -0.067 m | -0.013 |
| 10 m/s | broadside_separated | 5.099 m | 0.047 m | 0.009 |
| 20 m/s | aligned | 20.394 m | -1.004 m | -0.049 |
| 20 m/s | broadside_separated | 20.394 m | 0.695 m | 0.034 |
| 30 m/s | aligned | 45.887 m | -2.340 m | -0.051 |
| 30 m/s | broadside_separated | 45.887 m | 1.620 m | 0.035 |

Sensor-only altitude noise is centimeters to decimeters, while pressure-port aerodynamic bias can easily be meters at FPV speed. The current dynamic-pressure coefficients are equivalent to a few percent of dynamic pressure in aligned flow, which is plausible as a static-port placement/propwash abstraction but should not be described as raw barometer sensor noise.

## Betaflight blackbox timing and RPM telemetry anchors

Sources: [Betaflight blackbox source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/betaflight/betaflight/master/src/main/blackbox/blackbox.c), [blackbox-library parser fixture](https://github.com/maxlaverse/blackbox-library), [public Betaflight issue log](https://github.com/betaflight/betaflight/files/5507542/LOG00078.TXT), and [Betaflight PR #12562 RPM logs](https://github.com/betaflight/betaflight/pull/12562). Generated CSVs: `docs/data/blackbox_log_header_summary.csv`, `docs/data/blackbox_rpm_log_reference.csv`, `docs/data/blackbox_rpm_decoded_summary.csv`, and `docs/data/blackbox_rpm_decoded_samples.csv`, plus `docs/data/blackbox_rpm_response_model_comparison.csv`, and `docs/data/blackbox_rpm_filter_frequency_reference.csv`, and `docs/data/blackbox_gyro_rpm_spectrum_reference.csv`.

| Log source | firmware | fields | gyro | motor cmd | eRPM | looptime | PID denom | estimated main rate | DShot bidir | RPM notch |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| [Betaflight issue LOG00078](https://github.com/betaflight/betaflight/files/5507542/LOG00078.TXT) | Betaflight 4.2.4 (fbcaf8c50) STM32F411 | 34 | 1 | 1 | 0 | 125 us | 2 | 4000 Hz | 1 | 3 harmonics, LPF 150 Hz |
| [blackbox-library normal.bfl](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/maxlaverse/blackbox-library/master/fixtures/normal.bfl) | Betaflight 4.0.0 (173e958da) MATEKF405 | 38 | 1 | 1 | 0 | n/a us | 1 | n/a Hz | n/a | n/a harmonics, LPF n/a Hz |

The older public Betaflight issue log is useful because it is a real Betaflight 4.2.4 header with DShot bidirectional telemetry and RPM-filter settings enabled, but it does not expose RPM fields in the main field list. Betaflight PR #12562 fills that source gap with raw `.bbl` attachments whose headers expose `RPM[0..3]` or `eInterval[0..3]`; those binary frames are now decoded into summary and downsampled CSVs, though flight-context gyro/propwash fitting still needs richer logs.

Decoded RPM/eInterval frame statistics use [orangebox](https://pypi.org/project/orangebox/) and the unit convention from [PR #12562 patch](https://github.com/betaflight/betaflight/pull/12562.patch): early `RPM[]` values are `eRPM/100`, while `eInterval[]` values are one electrical-revolution interval in microseconds.

The model comparison treats current `racingQuad.maxRPM / motor_tau` as a first-order spin-up slew proxy and `maxRPM / braking_tau_proxy` as the active-braking slew proxy. These logs are not controlled step tests, so ratios are order-of-magnitude checks.

Generated open bench packet CSV: `docs/data/esc_test_propbench_packet.csv`. It downloads [alspitz/esc_test](https://github.com/alspitz/esc_test) RCBenchmark/AutoQuad raw logs plus [fpv-geek/prop-bench](https://github.com/fpv-geek/prop-bench) and [VayuESC Studio](https://github.com/varun29ankuS/Vayu) protocol files, then mirrors 402 `esc_test_propbench_packet_*` rows into the global summary. This is adjacent bench evidence: all alspitz sample tests use a DALPROP T7056 three-blade 7-inch prop at 16 V, not a direct 5-inch FPV prop, and the RCBenchmark command timestamps are absent.

| Open bench evidence | metric | current comparison | tuning read |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| `esc_test` RCBenchmark rows | `67,972` samples / `6` tests | source is 7-inch static bench | useful thrust/RPM/current curve and observed-slew envelope |
| Static `T/omega^2` fit | P50 `4.45e-6 N/(rad/s)^2` | `3.07x` current `racingQuad.k` | larger 7-inch prop scale; do not transplant to 5-inch |
| Strongest +RPM slew | `253,619 rpm/s` over 50 ms | `0.392x` current spin-up proxy | current `motor_tau` remains faster than this open bench trace |
| Strongest -RPM slew | `272,067 rpm/s` over 50 ms | `0.131x` current active-braking proxy | supports the earlier warning that braking is likely too aggressive |
| High-RPM torque/QT | `0` valid fit samples | no `Q/T` support | keep using Tyto/UIUC/MQTB torque rows for yaw torque |
| PropBench protocol lead | max-thrust ramp `5 s`, hold `1 s`, accel ramp `1 s`, FC poll `200 ms` | schema only | useful target protocol for future direct 5-inch bench CSVs |
| Vayu protocol lead | step response `20% -> 80%`, `50 ms` response samples, general `100 ms` collection | schema only, `0` public raw runs found | useful AM32/CSV search lead; torque measurement still marked future work |

Generated motor-response packet CSV: `docs/data/motor_response_dynamics_packet.csv`. It condenses RotorS/PX4 actuator lag, Betaflight PR #12562 decoded RPM slews, APdrone urban bidirectional-DShot eRPM timing, AI-IO low-dynamic hover-RPM scale, and the current ESC/braking formulas into 210 narrow metrics. Those rows are mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `motor_response_packet_*` categories.

| Motor-response evidence | observed/log metric | current comparison | tuning read |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| PR #12562 positive RPM slew | `503271` rpm/s max over 50 ms | `0.78x` current `racingQuad.maxRPM/motor_tau` proxy | spin-up tau is same-order for aggressive Betaflight RPM changes |
| PR #12562 negative RPM slew | `525478` rpm/s max over 50 ms | `0.254x` current active-braking proxy | current braking proxy is much stronger/faster than observed decel traces |
| APdrone command/RPM level lag | `47.9` ms P50 | current `apDrone` motor tau is `0.31x` lag | lag includes closed-loop command alignment, logging, and maneuver content |
| APdrone first-order tau candidate | `3.95` ms P50 across files | current `apDrone` motor tau is `3.80x` tau | useful as weak ESC/motor-response lower bound, not a final step-test fit |

## VRS and propwash descent-speed anchors

Generated VRS/propwash CSV: `docs/data/vrs_propwash_reference.csv`. The scan mirrors the current Java descent-ratio logic at zero transverse flow and separates VRS thrust loss from the earlier `propwash_start/full` handling disturbance.
Generated VRS/propwash calibration packet CSV: `docs/data/vrs_propwash_calibration_packet.csv`. It condenses reference anchors, Shetty/Selig digitized envelopes, current preset scans, and current-vs-reference comparisons into `1094` narrow metrics. These rows are mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `vrs_packet_*` categories.
Generated VRS time-history/source inventory CSV: `docs/data/vrs_time_history_source_inventory.csv`. It adds `168` narrow metrics for source traceability, Shetty/Selig record metadata, Stack/Leishman rotor-revolution timing, current amplitude ratios, and current RPM-to-Hz interval conversions. These rows are mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `vrs_time_*` categories.
Generated Shetty/Selig VRS digitization handoff CSV: `docs/data/vrs_shetty_digitization_packet.csv`. It adds `894` narrow metrics for source context, CT envelope points, mean CT loss, measured half-amplitude, `J`/`V/vi`/speed conversion, current-code comparisons, and frequency proxies. These rows are mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `vrs_digitization_packet_*` categories.
Generated NASA Johnson VRS regime packet CSV: `docs/data/vrs_johnson_regime_packet.csv`. It adds `272` narrow metrics for Johnson Table 4 parameters, current-preset boundary-speed conversions, current VRS/propwash interpolation at Johnson boundaries, and compact regime summaries. These rows are mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `vrs_johnson_packet_*` categories.
Generated side-by-side propeller VRS packet CSV: `docs/data/side_by_side_vrs_2026_packet.csv`. It adds `94` narrow metrics for the 2026 Physics of Fluids side-by-side propeller source, Table II vortex radius/circulation rows, co-rotating spacing trends, and current `racingQuad` adjacent-gap mapping. These rows are mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `side_by_side_vrs_packet_*` categories.

References: [Cambridge Flow dual-rotor axial-descent paper](https://www.cambridge.org/core/journals/flow/article/effects-of-rotor-separation-on-the-axial-descent-performance-of-dualrotor-configurations/BE7FE0D2E732E777CBD43F8E65CA0692), [2026 Physics of Fluids side-by-side propeller VRS paper](https://doi.org/10.1063/5.0311688), [NASA Johnson VRS model](https://rotorcraft.arc.nasa.gov/Publications/files/Johnson_TP-2005-213477.pdf), [NASA/Drexel multirotor vertical-descent wind-tunnel paper](https://researchdiscovery.drexel.edu/view/pdfCoverPage?download=true&filePid=13594340130004721&instCode=01DRXU_INST), [Shetty/Selig small-prop VRS paper](https://m-selig.ae.illinois.edu/pubs/ShettySelig-2011-AIAA-2011-1254-LRN-VSR-Props.pdf), [Shetty IDEALS thesis repository](https://www.ideals.illinois.edu/items/18490), [NASA Stack/Leishman model-rotor VRS report](https://ntrs.nasa.gov/citations/20040000835), [NASA Betzina tiltrotor VRS report](https://ntrs.nasa.gov/citations/20010062358), and [gym-pybullet-drones downwash formula](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/utiasDSL/gym-pybullet-drones/main/gym_pybullet_drones/envs/BaseAviary.py).

The VRS intensity thresholds line up with the literature-normalized descent band: the code reaches full-entry near `1.20 vi`, matching the low end of Cambridge's strongest measured loss/fluctuation band at `1.2-1.3 vi`. The current mean thrust-loss cap is close to the reported one-third peak-loss anchor, and the logged buffet envelope is just below Shetty/Selig's small-prop +/-30% fluctuation upper-bound. Stack/Leishman's rotor-revolution intervals suggest VRS buffet should stay a low-frequency aperiodic disturbance in the single-digit to low-tens Hz range for the current `racingQuad`, not a blade-pass vibration term. The separate `propwash_start/full` torque disturbance begins earlier and should remain a dirty-air handling tune unless propwash-specific blackbox or wind-tunnel torque data is added.

## Coaxial X8 spacing and wake-interference sanity

Open hardware/data source: [New Dexterity Coaxial Benchmarking Platform](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/newdexterity/Coaxial-Benchmarking-Platform/master/README.md); raw archive: [Data.rar](https://github.com/newdexterity/Coaxial-Benchmarking-Platform/blob/main/Data.rar); result log: [coaxial experiment notes](https://hackaday.io/project/181977/log/199225-some-results-of-coaxial-rotor-experiments-on-the-benchmarking-platform); paper DOI: [IEEE RA-L coaxial allocation paper](https://doi.org/10.1109/LRA.2022.3153999). Generated coaxial CSVs: `docs/data/coaxial_interference_reference.csv`, `docs/data/coaxial_benchmark_11in_target_efficiency.csv`, `docs/data/coaxial_benchmark_multi_size_target_efficiency.csv`, `docs/data/coaxial_benchmark_command_map_envelope.csv`, `docs/data/coaxial_runtime_allocation_lookup.csv`, `docs/data/coaxial_benchmark_surface_fit.csv`, and `docs/data/coaxial_allocation_calibration_packet.csv`.

Generated packet CSV: `docs/data/coaxial_allocation_calibration_packet.csv`. It mirrors into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `coaxial_packet_*` rows and should be used as a mixer/allocation prior, not a direct runtime controller, until the benchmark right/left channel convention is mapped to the project's upper/lower rotor ordering.

The current `coaxialX8` geometry uses `verticalOffset = 0.72R` above and below the arm plane, so the actual rotor-to-rotor separation is `1.44R = 0.72D`. That is inside the open benchmarking platform's reported tested distance range, making it a good next target for lower-rotor efficiency and wake-swirl calibration.

| 0.75 | 11.0in 910kv 11V propdrivev2 | 1.24 | 0.87/1.07 | 5.3% | 3.5% | 1.19/1.23/1.27 | 4.6%/5.5%/6.4% |
| 0.85 | 11.0in 910kv 11V propdrivev2 | 1.18 | 0.90/1.06 | 5.8% | 3.9% | 1.10/1.18/1.18 | 5.7%/6.2%/7.3% |

Generated command-surface fit CSV: `docs/data/coaxial_benchmark_surface_fit.csv`. Fits use cubic polynomial features in normalized PWM commands `u=(PWM-1000)/1000`; coefficient columns are named after the feature basis. CV columns use deterministic 5-fold splits over each 10x10 command map.

| Surface target | fits | median train RMSE/range | median CV RMSE/range | worst CV RMSE/range | median train/CV R2 | min CV R2 | worst CV max abs error |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| total_thrust_g | 29 | 0.72% | 1.07% | 5.61% | 0.9991/0.9979 | 0.9437 | 584.564 g |
| total_torque_nm | 29 | 0.84% | 1.06% | 7.70% | 0.9988/0.9982 | 0.8918 | 0.164 N*m |
| mechanical_power_w | 29 | 0.79% | 1.24% | 8.96% | 0.9988/0.9972 | 0.8744 | 136.719 W |
| electrical_power_w | 29 | 0.63% | 1.08% | 8.38% | 0.9993/0.9979 | 0.8880 | 174.149 W |

The Hackaday result log reports tests from `z/D = 0.1..1.0` in seven spacing points and 700 data points per rotor set. Its 11-inch rotor set shows mechanical-efficiency local maxima around `0.25 < z/D < 0.4` and `0.7 < z/D < 0.85`, with a local minimum near `z/D = 0.55`; the current X8 spacing of `z/D = 0.72` lands near the second local maximum. The same log notes that equal motor commands usually sit below the maximum-efficiency boundary, so a future X8 model should not assume upper/lower rotors are optimally efficient at equal command.

The raw Data.rar files make the qualitative result numerically useful: using measured torque and RPM, the 11-inch equal-command curve has local mechanical-efficiency peaks near the same z/D bands reported in the public log, while the current Java wake formula is mostly a smooth lower-rotor thrust-loss magnitude. The broader 11/16.2/22 inch comparison shows that best spacing and spread are load- and rotor-set-dependent, so a calibrated model should use an efficiency map or fitted surface rather than one monotonic separation scalar. The cubic fits are strongest for thrust, torque, and power; derive efficiency from fitted physical quantities instead of fitting noisy g/W values directly. The generated allocation-prior rows are ready for mixer experiments, but the current Java model still has no runtime term that consumes unequal-command gains.

## Battery internal-resistance anchors

Open aging/impedance datasets: [LiPo EIS dataset article](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC10518458/), [Mendeley direct dataset](https://data.mendeley.com/datasets/stcppt2r68/1), [Mendeley C-rate/temperature dataset](https://data.mendeley.com/datasets/kxsbr4x3j2/2), [NASA Li-ion aging datasets](https://data.nasa.gov/dataset/li-ion-battery-aging-datasets), and [NASA battery zip](https://phm-datasets.s3.amazonaws.com/NASA/5.+Battery+Data+Set.zip). FPV high-C context: [CHL LiPo IR explainer](https://chinahobbyline.com/blogs/news/lipo-internal-resistance-explained), [Oscar Liang 4S FPV LiPo charger-IR measurements](https://oscarliang.com/acehe-formula-4s-95c-lipo-batteries/), [Oscar Liang LiPo retirement/IR guide](https://oscarliang.com/when-retire-lipo-battery/), [Wayne Giles / Mark Forsyth LiPo ESR Meter Mark II guide](https://www.baronerosso.it/forum/attachments/batterie-e-caricabatterie/386965d1652293513-calcolo-c-di-scarica-lipo-meter.pdf), and [RC Helicopter Fun IR-based C formula](https://www.rchelicopterfun.com/lipo-internal-resistance.html).

| Preset | inferred cells | pack R | per-cell R | current limit | sag at limit |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | 4S | 0.018 ohm | 4.500 mOhm | 60.000 C | 1.620 V |
| cinewhoop | 4S | 0.035 ohm | 8.750 mOhm | 50.000 C | 2.275 V |
| heavyLift | 6S | 0.028 ohm | 4.667 mOhm | 28.000 C | 3.920 V |
| hexLift | 6S | 0.026 ohm | 4.333 mOhm | 26.667 C | 4.160 V |
| octoLift | 8S | 0.030 ohm | 3.750 mOhm | 27.500 C | 6.600 V |
| coaxialX8 | 8S | 0.030 ohm | 3.750 mOhm | 27.500 C | 6.600 V |

The CHL high-C LiPo guide gives practical per-cell IR bands: many new high-performance packs are around `2-5 mOhm`, below `10 mOhm` is a strong fresh-pack target, `10-20 mOhm` is still usable/healthy, and above `20 mOhm` is tired for high-performance use. Oscar Liang gives a more FPV-specific 1500mAh mini-quad threshold: below `10 mOhm/cell` is great, `10-15` is fine, `15-20` is old/high-resistance, and above `20` is a retire/relegate signal. Compare IR only at similar temperature, charge state, pack size, C rating, and cycle age.

| FPV 1500mAh IR health band | capacity range | per-cell IR range | Source |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| oscar_1500mah_great | 1.30-1.55 Ah | 0.000-10.000 mOhm/cell | [source](https://oscarliang.com/when-retire-lipo-battery/) |
| oscar_1500mah_fine | 1.30-1.55 Ah | 10.000-15.000 mOhm/cell | [source](https://oscarliang.com/when-retire-lipo-battery/) |
| oscar_1500mah_old | 1.30-1.55 Ah | 15.000-20.000 mOhm/cell | [source](https://oscarliang.com/when-retire-lipo-battery/) |
| oscar_1500mah_retire | 1.30-1.55 Ah | 20.000-inf mOhm/cell | [source](https://oscarliang.com/when-retire-lipo-battery/) |

The public 4S FPV charger-IR measurements below are not lab EIS data; the source reports charger readings at the end of charge on packs under 20 cycles. They are useful as absolute FPV-scale ESR anchors because NASA/Mendeley values are not high-C racing-pack absolute ESR.

|---|---:|---:|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|

| [Tattu 4S 45C 1550mAh](https://oscarliang.com/acehe-formula-4s-95c-lipo-batteries/) | 1.55 Ah / 45C | 6.525 mOhm | oscar_1500mah_great | 6.300/6.700 | 26.100 mOhm | 2.349 V | 0.400 mOhm |
| [Acehe Formula 4S 95C 1500mAh](https://oscarliang.com/acehe-formula-4s-95c-lipo-batteries/) | 1.50 Ah / 95C | 4.975 mOhm | oscar_1500mah_great | 4.800/5.100 | 19.900 mOhm | 1.791 V | 0.300 mOhm |

|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|

The current `racingQuad` `4.5 mOhm/cell` and all five Oscar-measured under-20-cycle 4S packs land in `oscar_1500mah_great`; `racingQuad` is still aggressive because it is `0.90x` the lowest measured row, Acehe Formula 4S 95C 1500mAh, and `0.69x` the measured Tattu 4S 45C 1550mAh row. Treat it as a fresh high-performance pack value, not a generic 4S FPV default.

Generated LiPo ESR temperature/SOC method CSV: `docs/data/lipo_esr_temperature_soc_method_reference.csv`. It encodes ESR-meter guidance to compare packs near `23 C / 72 F`, keep temperature and SOC separate, expect a 10 C drop to nearly double IR, and treat SOC below about `10%` as a different high-IR regime. It also applies the conservative IR-based `true C = 2500 / sqrt(capacity_mAh * highest_cell_IR_mOhm)` formula to current presets using configured mean per-cell IR as a proxy. These rows are mirrored into `docs/data/fpv_model_validation_summary.csv` as `lipo_esr_*` categories.

| Preset ESR formula check | configured cell IR | configured limit | formula true C/current | configured / formula | configured / 10C-cold guardrail |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| racingQuad | `4.50 mOhm` | `60.0 C / 90 A` | `30.43 C / 45.64 A` | `1.97x` | `2.79x` |
| cinewhoop | `8.75 mOhm` | `50.0 C / 65 A` | `23.44 C / 30.47 A` | `2.13x` | `3.02x` |
| heavyLift | `4.67 mOhm` | `28.0 C / 140 A` | `16.37 C / 81.83 A` | `1.71x` | `2.42x` |
| hexLift | `4.33 mOhm` | `26.7 C / 160 A` | `15.50 C / 93.03 A` | `1.72x` | `2.43x` |
| octoLift/coaxialX8 | `3.75 mOhm` | `27.5 C / 220 A` | `14.43 C / 115.47 A` | `1.91x` | `2.69x` |
| apDrone | `4.00 mOhm` | `100.0 C / 150 A` | `32.27 C / 48.41 A` | `3.10x` | `4.38x` |

Read this as a conservative sustained-current and cold-sag warning, not as a hard burst-current ban. The remaining ideal source is still a direct FPV high-C pack ESR sweep versus temperature, SOC, and cycle age.

Generated Mendeley C-rate/temperature inventory CSV: `docs/data/mendeley_c_rate_temperature_file_inventory.csv`. It records the full public `kxsbr4x3j2` dataset metadata: `334` files, `325` xlsx files, `638.23 MB`, DOI `10.17632/kxsbr4x3j2.2`, CC BY 4.0. The script caches only a selected `84.68 MB` subset locally instead of mirroring the full dataset.
Generated C-rate/temperature subset CSV: `docs/data/lipo_c_rate_temperature_subset_reference.csv`. Generated packet CSV: `docs/data/lipo_c_rate_temperature_calibration_packet.csv`. The packet condenses `33` selected k1 discharge curves and `22` temperature-ratio rows into `502` narrow metrics mirrored as `lipo_crate_packet_*`.

| Selected C-rate/temperature curve | capacity | average V | temp rise | mid-discharge R proxy vs 0.05C |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| NCA 2C 25 C | `2.964 Ah` | `3.050 V` | `17.19 C` | `94.73 mOhm` |

| 5 C vs 25 C temperature ratio | capacity ratio | V50 delta | initial R proxy ratio |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| NCA 2C | `0.616x` | `-0.054 V` | `1.401x` |
| NMC 2C | `0.830x` | `-0.209 V` | `1.150x` |
| LFP 2C | `0.893x` | `-0.211 V` | `1.147x` |
| LFP 20C | `0.00449x` | `-0.240 V` | `1.079x` |

The Mendeley C-rate/temperature rows are cylindrical NCA/NMC/LFP cell evidence, not FPV LiPo pouch-pack absolute ESR. Their strongest use here is shape: cold and high C-rate can sharply reduce delivered capacity and terminal voltage, and high-rate rows generate large surface-temperature rise. Current `racingQuad` is configured at `60C`, which is `30x` the NCA/NMC selected max and `3x` the LFP selected max, so this packet should guide limiter shape and caution around C-ratings rather than directly setting a 60C FPV pack resistance.

Generated APdrone battery-resistance envelope CSV: `docs/data/apdrone_battery_resistance_envelope.csv`. It reuses the APdrone battery-autonomy logs and compares current-scale assumptions against the current `apDrone()` `0.016 ohm` pack resistance.

| APdrone cross-scenario proxy | raw per amp normal/max | inferred pack R | inferred cell IR | config R / proxy | observed delta / config sag |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Betaflight literal logged centiamps | 100.000 / 100.000 | 0.1106 ohm | 27.655 mOhm | 0.145x | 6.914x |
| Foxeer official scale70 from logged scale400 | 17.500 / 17.500 | 0.0194 ohm | 4.840 mOhm | 0.826x | 1.210x |
| Round capacity candidate raw_per_amp20 | 20.000 / 20.000 | 0.0221 ohm | 5.531 mOhm | 0.723x | 1.383x |
| Scenario capacity match 1500mAh | 17.611 / 19.725 | 0.0234 ohm | 5.848 mOhm | 0.684x | 1.462x |

At APdrone's configured `150 A` limit, current `0.016 ohm` predicts `2.400 V` pack sag. The Oscar measured 4S rows would sag `2.985..4.110 V` at the same current, so `apDrone()` should be treated as a low-IR fresh-pack assumption unless direct APdrone battery DCIR/ACIR data is found.
