The current OCV curve is a configurable LiPo-shaped lookup between each preset's `emptyBatteryVoltage` and `nominalBatteryVoltage`. CALCE shows the real OCV curve is not the same thing as cutoff voltage; NASA's loaded discharge rows further separate rest OCV from terminal voltage under current. Keep OCV shape, ESR/sag, and SOC power limiting as separate calibration knobs.

Generated battery dynamic-pulse CSV: `docs/data/battery_dynamic_pulse_response_reference.csv`. It parses CALCE SP20-2 DST dynamic profiles at 0 C, 25 C, and 45 C for 50%/80% nominal SOC and fits rest-recovery time scales after charge/discharge steps.

| CALCE SP20-2 DST discharge recovery | pulse current | initial step R | first-rest recovery | total rest recovery | first sample fraction | tau 63% | tau log-fit | sample dt |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 50% SOC | -1.000 A | 79.634 mOhm | 0.077 V | 0.107 V | 0.718 | 630 s | 2150 s | 10.0 s |
| 80% SOC | -1.000 A | 80.286 mOhm | 0.082 V | 0.106 V | 0.771 | 79 s | 1676 s | 10.0 s |

| Current `racingQuad` battery transient tau | value |
|---|---:|
| Sag rise | 0.057 s |
| Sag recovery | 0.750 s |
| Voltage spike rise | 0.015 s |
| Voltage spike recovery | 0.143 s |
| Bus ripple rise | 0.006 s |
| Bus ripple recovery | 0.044 s |
| Current-limit attack | 0.043 s |
| Current-limit recovery | 0.560 s |

The CALCE DST recovery rows make a useful separation-of-physics check: slow rest relaxation is minutes-to-hours in these low-C Li-ion tests, while the current Java sag/spike/ripple filters are subsecond electrical transients. If the sim wants visible long battery recovery after sustained load, that should be a separate polarization/hysteresis state instead of stretching the short sag filter.

Temperature references: [Battery University low/high-temperature discharge](https://batteryuniversity.com/article/bu-502-discharging-at-high-and-low-temperatures), [Battery University internal-resistance performance](https://batteryuniversity.com/article/bu-802a-how-does-rising-internal-resistance-affect-performance), [CHL LiPo IR explainer](https://chinahobbyline.com/blogs/news/lipo-internal-resistance-explained), [Jeffco Aeromodlers LiPo ESR temperature PDF](https://jeffcoaeromodlers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/Lithium-Polymer-Batteries-96-website.pdf), the Mendeley LiPo ECM dataset above, and the new [Mendeley C-rate/temperature discharge dataset](https://data.mendeley.com/datasets/kxsbr4x3j2/2). | 100 C | 1.17x | 0.65x | 0.45x | 0.021 ohm | 58.680 A | 1.901/1.239 V |

| RC LiPo temperature ESR row | warm/cold temp | warm/cold total IR | warm/cold per-cell IR | measured ratio | current model ratio | model/reference |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| GensAce 3S 1000mAh / ESR Meter | 21.7/5.6 C | 90.880/152.400 mOhm | 30.293/50.800 mOhm | 1.677x | 1.521x | 0.907x |
| GensAce 3S 1000mAh / iCharger 206B | 21.7/5.6 C | 120.000/233.000 mOhm | 40.000/77.667 mOhm | 1.942x | 1.521x | 0.783x |
| NanoTech 3S 1000mAh / ESR Meter | 21.7/5.6 C | 31.800/59.480 mOhm | 10.600/19.827 mOhm | 1.870x | 1.521x | 0.813x |
| NanoTech 3S 1000mAh / iCharger 206B | 21.7/5.6 C | 29.000/59.000 mOhm | 9.667/19.667 mOhm | 2.034x | 1.521x | 0.748x |
| SkyLipo 3S 1000mAh / ESR Meter | 21.7/5.6 C | 100.360/168.600 mOhm | 33.453/56.200 mOhm | 1.680x | 1.521x | 0.905x |
| SkyLipo 3S 1000mAh / iCharger 206B | 21.7/5.6 C | 137.000/258.000 mOhm | 45.667/86.000 mOhm | 1.883x | 1.521x | 0.808x |

The current temperature model is qualitatively aligned with Li-ion behavior: cold packs get higher effective resistance and lower current capability, while high temperature gradually reduces allowable power before hard thermal limiting. The Jeffco field rows add a useful RC LiPo temperature-ratio anchor: over the same 71F-to-42F drop, the current model under-predicts measured ESR growth. Treat the coefficients as conservative for cold small-pack sag until matched to FPV high-C pack ESR versus temperature.

Generated NASA impedance CSV: `docs/data/nasa_battery_impedance_reference.csv`. It parses the nested NASA/DASHlink battery-aging zip, de-duplicates repeated B0025-B0028 files by battery id, and links each impedance cycle to the nearest previous positive discharge capacity. NASA `Re` is the fitted ohmic/electrolyte term; `Rct` is charge-transfer resistance, so `Re+Rct` is a slower-load polarization bound rather than instantaneous sag ESR.

Parsed `1956` impedance cycles across `34` cells. The room high-SOH baseline median is `Re=61.999` mOhm/cell and `Re+Rct=164.266` mOhm/cell; those absolute values are 18650 lab-cell values, much higher than FPV high-C pack ESR, so use the scale columns as the transferable part.

The strongest first-to-last total-resistance growth in the parsed cell summaries is `1.62x` for `B0043`, while its final SOH row is `0.774` if a nearby positive discharge capacity was available.

| NASA lookup band | samples/cells | median SOH | median Re | median Rct | Re scale | Re+Rct scale | Re scale p10-p90 |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| room_10_35C / fresh_ge_0.95 | 297/27 | 0.981 | 61.999 mOhm | 100.266 mOhm | 1.000x | 1.000x | 0.652-1.988x |
| room_10_35C / used_0.85_0.95 | 355/19 | 0.892 | 62.237 mOhm | 83.891 mOhm | 1.004x | 0.893x | 0.779-1.647x |
| room_10_35C / aged_0.75_0.85 | 498/19 | 0.798 | 65.234 mOhm | 90.039 mOhm | 1.052x | 0.945x | 0.884-1.633x |
| room_10_35C / worn_lt_0.75 | 726/25 | 0.690 | 75.914 mOhm | 127.157 mOhm | 1.224x | 1.397x | 0.954-1.880x |

The Figshare dataset reports `16` mOhm max nominal 1 kHz internal resistance for the DUT and EIS every cycle at 100% SOC. It is closer to sustained high-current operation than NASA's aging protocols, but it is still cylindrical Li-ion cell data; use it as an impedance-growth and high-current-cycle shape source, then normalize to a measured FPV LiPo ESR.

NASA, Figshare, and Mendeley now give complementary resistance-shape checks: NASA separates `Re` and `Rct` on 18650 cells across aging protocols, Figshare adds high-current 18650 EIS every cycle, and Mendeley gives a direct `RO(SOC, SOH)` lookup for small LiPo pouch cells. All should be normalized onto a separately measured high-C FPV pack ESR before being used in runtime voltage sag.

The Mendeley LiPo dataset exposes raw capacity, partial-discharge, EIS, and fitted ECM CSVs. The fitted model files provide columns `SOC, R_0, R_1, Q_1, a_1, R_2, Q_2, a_2, Q, L`, so `R_0(SOC, SOH)` is a direct candidate for replacing a constant internal resistance with a state-dependent lookup. Caveat: the cells are 3.7 V, 1.1 Ah BAK LP-503562-IS-3 packs measured at 25 C, with 1 A standard discharge and 3 A stress discharge, so the dataset informs SOC/SOH shape more than FPV high-C absolute resistance.

Extracted ECM summary CSV: `docs/data/lipo_ecm_mendeley_r0_summary.csv`. Runtime SOC/SOH lookup CSV: `docs/data/lipo_ecm_mendeley_soc_soh_lookup.csv`. The archive download endpoint is `https://data.mendeley.com/datasets/stcppt2r68/1` -> `/public-api/zip/stcppt2r68/download/1`; the large zip is kept in the local temp directory. Note: the actual fitted CSV header uses `RO` for ohmic resistance.

Across `57` fitted-cycle files, mean `RO` spans `75.586-92.987` mOhm/cell, low-SOC `RO` is `0.997-1.070x` high-SOC `RO`, and fitted discharge capacity reaches minimum SOH `0.630`.

Use the lookup as a dimensionless resistance-shape prior: multiply `r0_scale_vs_fresh_high_soc_median` by a separately calibrated FPV pack ESR. The Mendeley absolute `RO` values are much higher than fresh high-C FPV cells because these are small 1.1 Ah BAK cells under the published lab protocol.

## Interpretation queue

1. Keep `racingQuad.thrustCoefficient` in the measured 5-inch FPV range unless an explicit unit-conversion layer is added; it changes RPM, blade-pass frequency, tip Mach, gyro notch placement, motor current mapping, and all vibration terms.
2. Re-run this report after changing rotor constants so telemetry labels such as RPM, tip Mach, blade-pass notch, and motor electrical estimates stay tied to physical units.
3. Keep `yawTorquePerThrustMeter` separate from thrust-coefficient tuning. The current 5-inch yaw value is close to RotorS/UIUC magnitude, while PX4 Iris uses a much larger 0.06 m constant.
4. Keep the VRS thrust-loss path tied to induced velocity ratio; the current code thresholds are close to the Cambridge axial-descent reference, while Shetty/Selig's +/-30% small-prop fluctuation anchor and Stack/Leishman's 20-50 rotor-revolution timing suggest the separate `propwash_start/full` handling-disturbance tune should stay distinct from mean thrust loss and blade-pass vibration.
5. Keep runtime linear damping separate from quadratic body drag in every generated packet. The corrected IMAV rows show `racingQuad` low-speed drag is close to the mass-fit target, while UZH-FPV/RATM speed envelopes remain reachable under base drag; future fitting should target residual aero, prop unloading, and deliberate gameplay damping separately.
6. Keep `RotorSpec.bladeCount` aligned with the prop family used for calibration; three-blade FPV presets should keep blade-pass vibration and gyro notch telemetry at 3x mechanical motor frequency. Use the STARMAC Fig. 9 rows as a flapping scale check, and use DJI Mini 2 vibration spectra only with the generated alias table because its sample rate cannot directly observe high FPV blade-pass frequencies.
7. Label sensor-noise parameters as electronics-only or residual vibration/noise-after-filtering. Current values are much larger than bare IMU datasheet RMS at the configured LPF bandwidths, which is plausible for FPV vibration but not for pure sensor electronics.
8. Keep physical turbulence and FPV dirty-air feel separate. The wind model now has a low-altitude Dryden-scaled turbulence component plus a reduced deterministic burble component for obstacle/wake feel.
9. Separate barometer silicon pressure noise from pressure-port/propwash/dynamic-pressure altitude bias. The former is centimeters-to-decimeters; the current high-speed flow model is meters and should be documented as aerodynamic/static-port error.
10. Keep battery temperature effects separate from SOC/SOH effects. Current low-temperature resistance/current scaling is directionally plausible; the new Mendeley C-rate/temperature packet supports strong cold/high-C limiting shape, but coefficient calibration still needs high-C FPV pouch-pack ESR versus temperature.
11. Treat public blackbox logs without RPM fields as timing/gyro/motor-command anchors only. Betaflight PR #12562 now provides decoded `RPM[0..3]`/`eInterval[0..3]` time-series summaries plus gyro/RPM spectrum checks; use the downsampled CSV for response-shape inspection and the raw `.bbl` files for any higher-resolution fitting.
12. Next data targets: validate the generated coaxial allocation prior in the runtime mixer, refine Shetty/Selig VRS fluctuation digitization with raw/time-history data beyond the new source-inventory/timing packet, add FPV high-C pouch-pack absolute ESR versus SOC/temperature beyond the new Li-ion C-rate/temperature shape packet, find FPV airframe coast-down/log-fit drag, and collect flight-context blackbox logs that combine RPM telemetry with gyro propwash recovery. The RPM-frequency and VRS interval tables can seed expected notch, blade-pass, and low-frequency buffet bands for that search.
